=== Example 0 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions, Provide your reasoning step by step and conclude with 'ANSWER:	True', 'ANSWER:	False', or 'ANSWER:	Uncertain'.


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if a worksheet is not dispensable. From premise 6, we know that a worksheet is either paper or is environment-friendly. If it is paper, then from premise 3, a worksheet is woodware, and from premise 2, a worksheet is dispensable. If it is environment-friendly, we know it is good from premise 5, but we know nothing about whether it is dispensable. Therefore, we don't know if a worksheet is dispensible or not, so the statement is uncertain.
ANSWER:	Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona. From premise 1, we know that a La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another if it receives more points. From premise 4, we know that in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona. Therefore, in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona, so Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona, so the statement is true.
ANSWER:	True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate the statement "if Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel laureate". Let's assume that Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner. This doesn't tell us anything about whether Amy is a Nobel laureate, so the statement isn't true, meaning it is either False or Uncertain. To distinguish between the two, notice that we could have a scenario where Amy is neither an Olympic gold medal winner nor a Nobel laureate. None of the premises are violated in this case. This means the statement must be false.
ANSWER:	False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
People in this club who perform in school talent shows often attend and are very engaged with school events.
People in this club either perform in school talent shows often or are inactive and disinterested community members.
People in this club who chaperone high school dances are not students who attend the school.
All people in this club who are inactive and disinterested members of their community chaperone high school dances.
All young children and teenagers in this club who wish to further their academic careers and educational opportunities are students who attend the school.
Bonnie is in this club and she either both attends and is very engaged with school events and is a student who attends the school or is not someone who both attends and is very engaged with school events and is not a student who attends the school.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Bonnie performs in school talent shows often.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
Let's think step by step. We need to determine if Bonnie performs in school talent shows often based on the given premises.

1. **Premise Analysis**:
   - Premise 1: People in this club who perform in school talent shows often attend and are very engaged with school events.
   - Premise 2: People in this club either perform in school talent shows often or are inactive and disinterested community members.
   - Premise 3: People in this club who chaperone high school dances are not students who attend the school.
   - Premise 4: All people in this club who are inactive and disinterested members of their community chaperone high school dances.
   - Premise 5: All young children and teenagers in this club who wish to further their academic careers and educational opportunities are students who attend the school.
   - Premise 6: Bonnie is in this club and she either both attends and is very engaged with school events and is a student who attends the school or is not someone who both attends and is very engaged with school events and is not a student who attends the school.

2. **Analyzing Bonnie's Status**:
   - According to Premise 6, Bonnie either:
     - Attends and is very engaged with school events and is a student who attends the school, or
     - Is not someone who attends and is very engaged with school events and is not a student who attends the school.
   
   - If Bonnie attends and is very engaged with school events and is a student who attends the school, then according to Premise 1, Bonnie performs in school talent shows often.
   - If Bonnie does not attend and is not very engaged with school events and is not a student who attends the school, then according to Premise 4, Bonnie must be an inactive and disinterested member of the community, and thus, according to Premise 2, she must perform in school talent shows often.

3. **Conclusion**:
   - In both scenarios, whether Bonnie attends and is very engaged with school events and is a student who attends the school, or she is not someone who attends and is very engaged with school events and is not a student who attends the school, it leads to the conclusion that Bonnie performs in school talent shows often.

Therefore, the conclusion follows from the premises.

ANSWER: True
Processed: True

Reference: Uncertain
========================================

=== Example 1 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions, Provide your reasoning step by step and conclude with 'ANSWER:	True', 'ANSWER:	False', or 'ANSWER:	Uncertain'.


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if a worksheet is not dispensable. From premise 6, we know that a worksheet is either paper or is environment-friendly. If it is paper, then from premise 3, a worksheet is woodware, and from premise 2, a worksheet is dispensable. If it is environment-friendly, we know it is good from premise 5, but we know nothing about whether it is dispensable. </EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona. From premise 1, we know that a La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another if it receives more points. From premise 4, we know that in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona. Therefore, in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona, so Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona, so the statement is true.
ANSWER:	True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.

This means the statement must be false.
ANSWER:	False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
People in this club who perform in school talent shows often attend and are very engaged with school events.
People in this club either perform in school talent shows often or are inactive and disinterested community members.
People in this club who chaperone high school dances are not students who attend the school.
All people in this club who are inactive and disinterested members of their community chaperone high school dances.
All young children and teenagers in this club who wish to further their academic careers and educational opportunities are students who attend the school.
Bonnie is in this club and she either both attends and is very engaged with school events and is a student who attends the school or is not someone who both attends and is very engaged with school events and is not a student who attends the school.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Bonnie is either both a young child or teenager who wishes to further her academic career and educational opportunities and chaperones high school dances or neither is a young child nor teenager who wishes to further her academic career and educational opportunities, then Bonnie is either a student who attends the school or is an inactive and disinterested member of the community.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
Let's break down the premises and the conclusion step by step.

### Step-by-Step Analysis

#### Premises:
1. People in this club who perform in school talent shows often attend and are very engaged with school events.
2. People in this club either perform in school talent shows often or are inactive and disinterested community members.
3. People in this club who chaperone high school dances are not students who attend the school.
4. All people in this club who are inactive and disinterested members of their community chaperone high school dances.
5. All young children and teenagers in this club who wish to further their academic careers and educational opportunities are students who attend the school.
6. Bonnie is in this club and she either both attends and is very engaged with school events and is a student who attends the school or is not someone who both attends and is very engaged with school events and is not a student who attends the school.

#### Conclusion:
If Bonnie is either both a young child or teenager who wishes to further her academic career and educational opportunities and chaperones high school dances or neither is a young child nor teenager who wishes to further her academic career and educational opportunities, then Bonnie is either a student who attends the school or is an inactive and disinterested member of the community.

### Translation into FOL

1. \( P(x) \rightarrow A(x) \land E(x) \)
   - If \( x \) performs in school talent shows, then \( x \) attends and is very engaged with school events.
2. \( P(x) \lor I(x) \)
   - If \( x \) is in the club, then \( x \) performs in school talent shows or is inactive and disinterested.
3. \( C(x) \rightarrow \neg S(x) \)
   - If \( x \) chaperones high school dances, then \( x \) is not a student who attends the school.
4. \( I(x) \rightarrow C(x) \)
   - If \( x \) is inactive and disinterested, then \( x \) chaperones high school dances.
5. \( Y(x) \land W(x) \rightarrow S(x) \)
   - If \( x \) is a young child or teenager and wishes to further their academic career and educational opportunities, then \( x \) is a student who attends the school.
6. \( B \rightarrow (A \land S) \lor (\neg A \land \neg S) \)
   - If Bonnie is in the club, then she either attends and is very engaged with school events and is a student who attends the school or does not attend and is not a student who attends the school.

### Evaluating the Conclusion

We need to check if the conclusion logically follows from the premises:

**Conclusion:**
\[ (Y(B) \land W(B) \land C(B)) \lor \neg (Y(B) \land W(B)) \rightarrow (S(B) \lor I(B)) \]

#### Case 1: \( Y(B) \land W(B) \land C(B) \)
- From premise 5: \( Y(B) \land W(B) \rightarrow S(B) \)
- From premise 3: \( C(B) \rightarrow \neg S(B) \)
- These two statements contradict each other. Therefore, \( Y(B) \land W(B) \land C(B) \) cannot be true simultaneously.

#### Case 2: \( \neg (Y(B) \land W(B)) \)
- If \( \neg (Y(B) \land W(B)) \), then Bonnie is either not a young child or teenager who wishes to further her academic career and educational opportunities.
- From premise 6: \( B \rightarrow (A \land S) \lor (\neg A \land \neg S) \)
- Since \( \neg (Y(B) \land W(B)) \), Bonnie is either not performing in school talent shows and not attending and being very engaged with school events, or she is not an inactive and disinterested member of the community.

Since the contradiction in Case 1 and the logical structure of Case 2 show that the conclusion holds under all possible scenarios, the conclusion logically follows from the premises.

### Final Answer
ANSWER: True
Processed: True

Reference: True
========================================

=== Example 2 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions, Provide your reasoning step by step and conclude with 'ANSWER:	True', 'ANSWER:	False', or 'ANSWER:	Uncertain'.


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if a worksheet is not dispensable. From premise 6, we know that a worksheet is either paper or is environment-friendly. If it is paper, then from premise 3, a worksheet is woodware, and from premise 2, a worksheet is dispensable. If it is environment-friendly, we know it is good from premise 5, but we know nothing about whether it is dispensable. Therefore, we don't know if a worksheet is dispensible or not, so the statement is uncertain.
ANSWER:	Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona. From premise 1, we know that a La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another if it receives more points. From premise 4, we know that in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona. Therefore, in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona, so Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona, so the statement is true.
ANSWER:	True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate the statement "if Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel laureate". Let's assume that Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner. This doesn't tell us anything about whether Amy is a Nobel laureate, so the statement isn't true, meaning it is either False or Uncertain. To distinguish between the two, notice that we could have a scenario where Amy is neither an Olympic gold medal winner nor a Nobel laureate. None of the premises are violated in this case. This means the statement must be false.
ANSWER:	False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
People in this club who perform in school talent shows often attend and are very engaged with school events.
People in this club either perform in school talent shows often or are inactive and disinterested community members.
People in this club who chaperone high school dances are not students who attend the school.
All people in this club who are inactive and disinterested members of their community chaperone high school dances.
All young children and teenagers in this club who wish to further their academic careers and educational opportunities are students who attend the school.
Bonnie is in this club and she either both attends and is very engaged with school events and is a student who attends the school or is not someone who both attends and is very engaged with school events and is not a student who attends the school.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Bonnie either chaperones high school dances or, if she does not, she performs in school talent shows often, then Bonnie is both a young child or teenager who wishes to further her academic career and educational opportunities and an inactive and disinterested member of the community.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
Let's analyze the premises and the conclusion step by step.

### Step-by-Step Analysis

1. **Premise 1**: People in this club who perform in school talent shows often attend and are very engaged with school events.
2. **Premise 2**: People in this club either perform in school talent shows often or are inactive and disinterested community members.
3. **Premise 3**: People in this club who chaperone high school dances are not students who attend the school.
4. **Premise 4**: All people in this club who are inactive and disinterested members of their community chaperone high school dances.
5. **Premise 5**: All young children and teenagers in this club who wish to further their academic careers and educational opportunities are students who attend the school.
6. **Premise 6**: Bonnie is in this club and she either both attends and is very engaged with school events and is a student who attends the school or is not someone who both attends and is very engaged with school events and is not a student who attends the school.

### Conclusion
The conclusion states:
"If Bonnie either chaperones high school dances or, if she does not, she performs in school talent shows often, then Bonnie is both a young child or teenager who wishes to further her academic career and educational opportunities and an inactive and disinterested member of the community."

### Reasoning

1. **From Premise 6**: Bonnie is either:
   - A student who attends the school and is very engaged with school events (and thus performs in school talent shows often), or
   - Not a student who attends the school and is not very engaged with school events (and thus is an inactive and disinterested community member).

2. **From Premise 4 and Premise 2**:
   - If Bonnie is an inactive and disinterested community member, she must chaperone high school dances (Premise 4).
   - If Bonnie chaperones high school dances, she cannot be a student who attends the school (Premise 3).

3. **Combining the above**:
   - If Bonnie is not a student who attends the school and is not very engaged with school events, she must chaperone high school dances (from Premise 4 and Premise 2).
   - If Bonnie chaperones high school dances, she cannot be a student who attends the school (from Premise 3).

4. **Conclusion Analysis**:
   - If Bonnie chaperones high school dances, she is an inactive and disinterested community member (from Premise 4).
   - If Bonnie does not chaperone high school dances, she must perform in school talent shows often (from Premise 2 and Premise 6).

5. **Checking the Conclusion**:
   - The conclusion states that if Bonnie either chaperones high school dances or, if she does not, she performs in school talent shows often, then she is both a young child or teenager who wishes to further her academic career and educational opportunities and an inactive and disinterested member of the community.
   - From our analysis, if Bonnie does not chaperone high school dances, she must perform in school talent shows often, but this does not necessarily mean she is a young child or teenager who wishes to further her academic career and educational opportunities (Premise 5 only applies to young children and teenagers in the club).

### Final Answer
Since the conclusion introduces additional conditions (being a young child or teenager who wishes to further her academic career and educational opportunities) that are not directly supported by the premises, the conclusion is not necessarily true based on the given information.

**ANSWER: False**
Processed: False

Reference: False
========================================

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.

<CONCLUSION>

This doesn't tell us anything about whether Amy is a Nobel laureate, so the statement isn't true, meaning it is either False or Uncertain. To distinguish between the two, notice that we could have a scenario where Amy is neither an Olympic gold medal winner nor a Nobel laureate. None of the premises are violated in this case. This means the statement must be false.
ANSWER:	False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All employees who schedule a meeting with their customers will go to the company building today.
Everyone who has lunch in the company building schedules meetings with their customers.
Employees have lunch either in the company building or at home.
If an employee has lunch at home, they are working remotely from home.
All employees who are in other countries work remotely from home.
No managers work remotely from home.
James will appear in the company today if and only if he is a manager.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
James has lunch in the company.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
Let's analyze the premises step by step to determine if the conclusion "James has lunch in the company" follows.

1. **Premise Analysis**:
   - All employees who schedule a meeting with their customers will go to the company building today.
   - Everyone who has lunch in the company building schedules meetings with their customers.
   - Employees have lunch either in the company building or at home.
   - If an employee has lunch at home, they are working remotely from home.
   - All employees who are in other countries work remotely from home.
   - No managers work remotely from home.
   - James will appear in the company today if and only if he is a manager.

2. **Determine James's Status**:
   - According to the last premise, James will appear in the company today if and only if he is a manager.
   - Since no managers work remotely from home, if James were working remotely from home, he would not be a manager.
   - Therefore, for James to be a manager, he must appear in the company today.

3. **Determine James's Lunch Location**:
   - If James appears in the company today, he cannot be working remotely from home.
   - Since employees have lunch either in the company building or at home, and James is not working remotely from home, he must have lunch in the company building.
   - If James has lunch in the company building, according to the second premise, he schedules meetings with his customers.
   - If James schedules meetings with his customers, according to the first premise, he will go to the company building today.

4. **Conclusion**:
   - The analysis shows that if James is a manager, he will appear in the company today, and since he cannot be working remotely from home, he must have lunch in the company building.
   - Therefore, James having lunch in the company is consistent with all the premises.

**Final Answer**: ANSWER: True
Processed: True

Reference: Uncertain

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.

</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona. From premise 1, we know that a La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another if it receives more points. From premise 4, we know that in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona. Therefore, in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona, so Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona, so the statement is true.
ANSWER:	True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate the statement "if Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel laureate". Let's assume that Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner. This doesn't tell us anything about whether Amy is a Nobel laureate, so the statement isn't true, meaning it is either False or Uncertain. To distinguish between the two, notice that we could have a scenario where Amy is neither an Olympic gold medal winner nor a Nobel laureate. None of the premises are violated in this case. This means the statement must be false.
ANSWER:	False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All employees who schedule a meeting with their customers will go to the company building today.
Everyone who has lunch in the company building schedules meetings with their customers.
Employees have lunch either in the company building or at home.
If an employee has lunch at home, they are working remotely from home.
All employees who are in other countries work remotely from home.
No managers work remotely from home.
James will appear in the company today if and only if he is a manager.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
James does not have lunch in the company.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if James does not have lunch in the company.

1. **Premise Analysis**:
   - All employees who schedule a meeting with their customers will go to the company building today.
   - Everyone who has lunch in the company building schedules meetings with their customers.
   - Employees have lunch either in the company building or at home.
   - If an employee has lunch at home, they are working remotely from home.
   - All employees who are in other countries work remotely from home.
   - No managers work remotely from home.
   - James will appear in the company today if and only if he is a manager.

2. **Logical Deductions**:
   - From the last premise, if James appears in the company today, he is a manager.
   - From the second premise, if someone has lunch in the company building, they schedule meetings with their customers.
   - From the first premise, if someone schedules meetings with their customers, they will go to the company building today.
   - Combining these, if James has lunch in the company building, he will go to the company building today and schedule meetings with his customers, making him a manager.
   - From the seventh premise, if James is a manager, he will appear in the company today.
   - From the sixth premise, no managers work remotely from home, so if James is a manager, he cannot be working remotely from home.
   - From the fifth premise, if James is working remotely from home, he must be in another country.
   - Since James cannot be both in the company and in another country simultaneously, he cannot be a manager and thus cannot appear in the company today.
   - Therefore, James cannot have lunch in the company building because if he did, he would have to be a manager and appear in the company today, which contradicts the fact that he does not appear in the company today.

3. **Conclusion**:
   - Since James does not appear in the company today, he cannot be a manager.
   - If James is not a manager, he cannot have lunch in the company building because having lunch in the company building implies scheduling meetings, which would make him a manager.
   - Therefore, James does not have lunch in the company building.

ANSWER: True
Processed: True

Reference: Uncertain

=== Example 5 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions, Provide your reasoning step by step and conclude with 'ANSWER:	True', 'ANSWER:	False', or 'ANSWER:	Uncertain'.


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if a worksheet is not dispensable. From premise 6, we know that a worksheet is either paper or is environment-friendly. If it is paper, then from premise 3, a worksheet is woodware, and from premise 2, a worksheet is dispensable. If it is environment-friendly, we know it is good from premise 5, but we know nothing about whether it is dispensable. Therefore, we don't know if a worksheet is dispensible or not, so the statement is uncertain.
ANSWER:	Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona. From premise 1, we know that a La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another if it receives more points. From premise 4, we know that in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona. Therefore, in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona, so Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona, so the statement is true.
ANSWER:	True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate the statement "if Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel laureate". Let's assume that Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner. This doesn't tell us anything about whether Amy is a Nobel laureate, so the statement isn't true, meaning it is either False or Uncertain. To distinguish between the two, notice that we could have a scenario where Amy is neither an Olympic gold medal winner nor a Nobel laureate. None of the premises are violated in this case. This means the statement must be false.
ANSWER:	False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All employees who schedule a meeting with their customers will go to the company building today.
Everyone who has lunch in the company building schedules meetings with their customers.
Employees have lunch either in the company building or at home.
If an employee has lunch at home, they are working remotely from home.
All employees who are in other countries work remotely from home.
No managers work remotely from home.
James will appear in the company today if and only if he is a manager.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If James is either a manager or in other countries,  then James does not either has lunch at home or work remotely from home. If James either has lunch at home or works remotely from home, then he is neither a manager nor does he work in other countries. [contrapositive is more natural]
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
Let's break down the problem step by step.

First, let's translate the premises into first-order logic (FOL) expressions:

1. \( \forall x (E(x) \rightarrow S(x)) \) - All employees who schedule a meeting with their customers will go to the company building today.
2. \( \forall x (C(x) \rightarrow M(x)) \) - Everyone who has lunch in the company building schedules meetings with their customers.
3. \( \forall x (L(x) \rightarrow (B(x) \lor H(x))) \) - Employees have lunch either in the company building or at home.
4. \( \forall x ((H(x) \land \neg B(x)) \rightarrow R(x)) \) - If an employee has lunch at home, they are working remotely from home.
5. \( \forall x ((\neg B(x) \land \neg H(x)) \rightarrow O(x)) \) - All employees who are in other countries work remotely from home.
6. \( \forall x (\neg M(x) \rightarrow \neg R(x)) \) - No managers work remotely from home.
7. \( \forall x (J(x) \leftrightarrow M(x)) \) - James will appear in the company today if and only if he is a manager.

Now, let's translate the conclusion into a FOL expression:
\[ (M(J) \lor O(J)) \rightarrow \neg (H(J) \lor R(J)) \]
\[ (H(J) \lor R(J)) \rightarrow \neg (M(J) \lor O(J)) \]

We need to determine if these two statements are logically equivalent based on the given premises.

### Step-by-Step Analysis

1. **Assume \( M(J) \lor O(J) \):**
   - If \( M(J) \), then \( \neg R(J) \) (from premise 6).
   - If \( O(J) \), then \( R(J) \) (from premise 5).

   Since \( M(J) \lor O(J) \), we have two cases:
   - Case 1: \( M(J) \)
     - Then \( \neg R(J) \).
     - So, \( \neg (H(J) \lor R(J)) \) is true because \( R(J) \) is false.
   - Case 2: \( O(J) \)
     - Then \( R(J) \).
     - So, \( \neg (H(J) \lor R(J)) \) is false because \( R(J) \) is true.

   Therefore, \( (M(J) \lor O(J)) \rightarrow \neg (H(J) \lor R(J)) \) is not always true.

2. **Assume \( H(J) \lor R(J) \):**
   - If \( H(J) \), then \( R(J) \) (from premise 4).
   - If \( R(J) \), then \( \neg M(J) \) (from premise 6).

   Since \( H(J) \lor R(J) \), we have two cases:
   - Case 1: \( H(J) \)
     - Then \( R(J) \).
     - So, \( \neg (M(J) \lor O(J)) \) is true because \( M(J) \) is false and \( O(J) \) is false.
   - Case 2: \( R(J) \)
     - Then \( \neg M(J) \).
     - So, \( \neg (M(J) \lor O(J)) \) is true because \( M(J) \) is false.

   Therefore, \( (H(J) \lor R(J)) \rightarrow \neg (M(J) \lor O(J)) \) is always true.

Since the second part of the conclusion is always true, but the first part is not always true, the overall statement is not logically equivalent.

### Conclusion
The conclusion is not logically equivalent to the given premises.

**ANSWER: False**
Processed: False

Reference: True

7. \( \forall x (Monkeypox(x) \rightarrow \text{HasSymptoms}(x, \text{muscle pains})) \)
8. \( \forall x (Monkeypox(x) \rightarrow \text{HasSymptoms}(x, \text{tiredness})) \)
9. \( \text{Human}(z) \rightarrow \text{Feeling}(z, \text{tired}) \)
10. \( \text{Feeling}(w, \text{coughing}) \rightarrow \text{Cause}(w, \text{flu}) \)

From these premises, we can see that the only explicit symptoms of Monkeypox mentioned are fever, headache, muscle pains, and tiredness. There is no information provided that directly links coughing to Monkeypox.

Therefore, based on the given premises, we cannot conclude that symptoms of Monkeypox include coughing.

</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
The Legend of Zelda is on the Top 10 list.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:

1. **Premise 1**: A Japanese game company created the game The Legend of Zelda.
   - This tells us who created the game but does not directly relate to its placement on the Top 10 list.

2. **Premise 2**: All games on the Top 10 list are made by Japanese game companies.
   - This implies that any game on the Top 10 list must have been created by a Japanese game company. However, it does not guarantee that all games made by Japanese companies are on the list.

3. **Premise 3**: If a game sells more than one million copies, then it will be included in the Top 10 list.
   - This gives us a condition for inclusion in the Top 10 list based on sales.

4. **Premise 4**: The Legend of Zelda sold more than one million copies.
   - This tells us that The Legend of Zelda meets the sales criterion for being on the Top 10 list.

Given these premises:
- Since The Legend of Zelda sold more than one million copies (Premise 4), according to Premise 3, it should be included in the Top 10 list.
- Additionally, since it was created by a Japanese game company (Premise 1), and all games on the Top 10 list are made by Japanese game companies (Premise 2), it satisfies the conditions for being on the list.

Therefore, based on the given premises, The Legend of Zelda is on the Top 10 list.

ANSWER: True
Processed: True

   - Conclusion: The Legend of Zelda is not on the Top 10 list.

3. **Reasoning**:
   - From Premise 4, we know that The Legend of Zelda sold more than one million copies.
   - According to Premise 3, any game that sells more than one million copies will be included in the Top 10 list.
   - Therefore, The Legend of Zelda should be on the Top 10 list based on its sales.
   - Premise 2 states that all games on the Top 10 list are made by Japanese game companies.
   - Premise 1 confirms that The Legend of Zelda was created by a Japanese game company.
   - Since The Legend of Zelda meets the criteria for being on the Top 10 list (both in terms of sales and company origin), it must be on the list.

Given the above reasoning, the conclusion that "The Legend of Zelda is not on the Top 10 list" contradicts the premises provided.

ANSWER: False
Processed: False

Reference: False

=== Example 15 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions, Provide your reasoning step by step and conclude with 'ANSWER:	True', 'ANSWER:	False', or 'ANSWER:	Uncertain'.

All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

If it is paper, then from premise 3, a worksheet is woodware, and from premise 2, a worksheet is dispensable. If it is environment-friendly, we know it is good from premise 5, but we know nothing about whether it is dispensable. Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

From premise 4, we know that in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona. Therefore, in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona, so Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona, so the statement is true.
ANSWER:	True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.

No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.

If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>

To distinguish between the two, notice that we could have a scenario where Amy is neither an Olympic gold medal winner nor a Nobel laureate. None of the premises are violated in this case. This means the statement must be false.
ANSWER:	False
</EVALUATE>

   - This means any object that has four sides is considered a shape.

3. **Conclusion**: All squares are shapes.
   - To determine if this conclusion is valid, we need to see if every square, based on the premises, can be classified as a shape.

From Premise 1, we know that all squares have four sides. According to Premise 2, all four-sided things are shapes. Therefore, since squares are four-sided, they must be shapes.

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona. From premise 1, we know that a La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another if it receives more points. From premise 4, we know that in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona. Therefore, in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona, so Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona, so the statement is true.
ANSWER:	True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate the statement "if Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel laureate". Let's assume that Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner. This doesn't tell us anything about whether Amy is a Nobel laureate, so the statement isn't true, meaning it is either False or Uncertain. To distinguish between the two, notice that we could have a scenario where Amy is neither an Olympic gold medal winner nor a Nobel laureate. None of the premises are violated in this case. This means the statement must be false.
ANSWER:	False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All rabbits that can be spotted near the campus are cute.
Some turtles can be spotted near the campus.
The only animals that can be spotted near the campus are rabbits and squirrels.
If something is skittish, then it is not calm.
All the squirrels that can be spotted near the campus are skittish.
Rockie can be spotted near the campus, and it is calm.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Rockie is not both a turtle and a squirrel, then Rockie is either cute or skittish.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
Let's analyze the premises and conclusion step by step.

### Step-by-Step Analysis

1. **Premises:**
   - All rabbits that can be spotted near the campus are cute.
   - Some turtles can be spotted near the campus.
   - The only animals that can be spotted near the campus are rabbits and squirrels.
   - If something is skittish, then it is not calm.
   - All the squirrels that can be spotted near the campus are skittish.
   - Rockie can be spotted near the campus, and it is calm.

2. **Conclusion:**
   - If Rockie is not both a turtle and a squirrel, then Rockie is either cute or skittish.

### Translation into First-Order Logic

- Let \( R(x) \) denote "x is a rabbit."
- Let \( T(x) \) denote "x is a turtle."
- Let \( S(x) \) denote "x is a squirrel."
- Let \( C(x) \) denote "x can be spotted near the campus."
- Let \( U(x) \) denote "x is cute."
- Let \( K(x) \) denote "x is skittish."
- Let \( L(x) \) denote "x is calm."

From the premises:
1. \( \forall x (C(x) \rightarrow R(x)) \)
2. \( \exists x (T(x) \land C(x)) \)
3. \( \forall x (C(x) \rightarrow (R(x) \lor S(x))) \)
4. \( \forall x (K(x) \rightarrow \neg L(x)) \)
5. \( \forall x (S(x) \land C(x) \rightarrow K(x)) \)
6. \( C(\text{Rockie}) \)
7. \( L(\text{Rockie}) \)

### Reasoning

From premise 6 and 7, we know:
- \( C(\text{Rockie}) \)
- \( L(\text{Rockie}) \)

Using premise 4, since \( L(\text{Rockie}) \), we get:
\[ \neg K(\text{Rockie}) \]

Using premise 5, since \( \neg K(\text{Rockie}) \), we get:
\[ \neg (S(\text{Rockie}) \land C(\text{Rockie})) \]
This simplifies to:
\[ \neg S(\text{Rockie}) \lor \neg C(\text{Rockie}) \]
Since \( C(\text{Rockie}) \) is true, we have:
\[ \neg S(\text{Rockie}) \]

Now, using premise 3, since \( C(\text{Rockie}) \):
\[ C(\text{Rockie}) \rightarrow (R(\text{Rockie}) \lor S(\text{Rockie})) \]
Given \( \neg S(\text{Rockie}) \), we get:
\[ R(\text{Rockie}) \]

Finally, using premise 1, since \( R(\text{Rockie}) \):
\[ U(\text{Rockie}) \]

Thus, if Rockie is not both a turtle and a squirrel, then Rockie is either cute or skittish. Since \( R(\text{Rockie}) \) implies \( U(\text{Rockie}) \), the conclusion holds true.

### Conclusion

ANSWER: True
Processed: True

Reference: True
========================================

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if a worksheet is not dispensable. From premise 6, we know that a worksheet is either paper or is environment-friendly. If it is paper, then from premise 3, a worksheet is woodware, and from premise 2, a worksheet is dispensable. If it is environment-friendly, we know it is good from premise 5, but we know nothing about whether it is dispensable. Therefore, we don't know if a worksheet is dispensible or not, so the statement is uncertain.
ANSWER:	Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona. From premise 1, we know that a La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another if it receives more points. From premise 4, we know that in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona. Therefore, in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona, so Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona, so the statement is true.
ANSWER:	True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate the statement "if Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel laureate". Let's assume that Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner. This doesn't tell us anything about whether Amy is a Nobel laureate, so the statement isn't true, meaning it is either False or Uncertain. To distinguish between the two, notice that we could have a scenario where Amy is neither an Olympic gold medal winner nor a Nobel laureate. None of the premises are violated in this case. This means the statement must be false.
ANSWER:	False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All rabbits that can be spotted near the campus are cute.
Some turtles can be spotted near the campus.
The only animals that can be spotted near the campus are rabbits and squirrels.
If something is skittish, then it is not calm.
All the squirrels that can be spotted near the campus are skittish.
Rockie can be spotted near the campus, and it is calm.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Rockie is cute and calm, then Rockie is a skittish turtle.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
Let's analyze the given premises and conclusion step by step.

### Step-by-Step Analysis

1. **Premise 1**: All rabbits that can be spotted near the campus are cute.
   - Symbolically: \( \forall x (Rabbit(x) \land SpottedNearCampus(x) \rightarrow Cute(x)) \)

2. **Premise 2**: Some turtles can be spotted near the campus.
   - Symbolically: \( \exists x (Turtle(x) \land SpottedNearCampus(x)) \)

3. **Premise 3**: The only animals that can be spotted near the campus are rabbits and squirrels.
   - Symbolically: \( \forall x (SpottedNearCampus(x) \rightarrow (Rabbit(x) \lor Squirrel(x))) \)

4. **Premise 4**: If something is skittish, then it is not calm.
   - Symbolically: \( \forall x (Skittish(x) \rightarrow \neg Calm(x)) \)

5. **Premise 5**: All the squirrels that can be spotted near the campus are skittish.
   - Symbolically: \( \forall x (Squirrel(x) \land SpottedNearCampus(x) \rightarrow Skittish(x)) \)

6. **Premise 6**: Rockie can be spotted near the campus, and it is calm.
   - Symbolically: \( SpottedNearCampus(Rockie) \land Calm(Rockie) \)

7. **Conclusion**: If Rockie is cute and calm, then Rockie is a skittish turtle.
   - Symbolically: \( (Cute(Rockie) \land Calm(Rockie)) \rightarrow Turtle(Rockie) \land Skittish(Rockie) \)

### Reasoning

1. **From Premise 6**:
   - \( SpottedNearCampus(Rockie) \)
   - \( Calm(Rockie) \)

2. **From Premise 3**:
   - Since \( Rockie \) can be spotted near the campus, \( Rockie \) must be either a rabbit or a squirrel.
     - \( SpottedNearCampus(Rockie) \rightarrow (Rabbit(Rockie) \lor Squirrel(Rockie)) \)

3. **From Premise 6 and Premise 4**:
   - Since \( Rockie \) is calm, it cannot be skittish.
     - \( Calm(Rockie) \rightarrow \neg Skittish(Rockie) \)

4. **From Premise 5**:
   - If \( Rockie \) were a squirrel, it would be skittish.
     - \( Squirrel(Rockie) \rightarrow Skittish(Rockie) \)
   - But since \( Rockie \) is not skittish, \( Rockie \) cannot be a squirrel.
     - \( \neg Squirrel(Rockie) \)

5. **From Premise 3 and the above**:
   - Since \( Rockie \) is not a squirrel, \( Rockie \) must be a rabbit.
     - \( Rabbit(Rockie) \)

6. **From Premise 1**:
   - Since \( Rockie \) is a rabbit and can be spotted near the campus, \( Rockie \) is cute.
     - \( Rabbit(Rockie) \land SpottedNearCampus(Rockie) \rightarrow Cute(Rockie) \)

7. **Conclusion Check**:
   - Given \( Rockie \) is cute and calm, we need to check if \( Rockie \) is a skittish turtle.
     - \( (Cute(Rockie) \land Calm(Rockie)) \rightarrow Turtle(Rockie) \land Skittish(Rockie) \)
   - From our previous steps, we know \( Rockie \) is a rabbit and not skittish.
     - \( \neg Skittish(Rockie) \)

Since \( Rockie \) is not skittish, the conclusion \( (Cute(Rockie) \land Calm(Rockie)) \rightarrow Turtle(Rockie) \land Skittish(Rockie) \) is false.

### Final Answer
ANSWER: False
Processed: False

Reference: False
========================================

   - If and only if Karen binge-watches a Netflix show, she will download it.
   - Karen does not download "Black Mirror."
   - "Black Mirror" is a Netflix show.
   - If Karen binge-watches a Netflix show, she will share it with Lisa.

2. **Deductions**:
   - Since "Stranger Things" is a popular Netflix show (Premise 1), according to Premise 2, Karen will binge-watch "Stranger Things."
   - According to Premise 3, if Karen binge-watches "Stranger Things," she will download it.
   - According to Premise 6, if Karen binge-watches a Netflix show, she will share it with Lisa. Since "Stranger Things" is a Netflix show and Karen will binge-watch it, she will share it with Lisa.

Therefore, based on the logical flow of the premises, we can conclude that Karen will indeed share "Stranger Things" with Lisa.

<PREMISES>
All aliens are extraterrestrials.
If someone is from Mars, then they are an alien.
No extraterrestrials are human.
All highly intelligent beings from Earth are humans.
Marvin is a highly intelligent being.
Marvin is either from Earth and from Mars, or he is from neither.
If Marvin is not from Earth, then Marvin is an extraterrestrial.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Marvin is an alien.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
Let's think step by step. We want to determine if Marvin is an alien based on the given premises.

1. **Premise Analysis**:
   - All aliens are extraterrestrials.
   - If someone is from Mars, then they are an alien.
   - No extraterrestrials are human.
   - All highly intelligent beings from Earth are humans.
   - Marvin is a highly intelligent being.
   - Marvin is either from Earth and from Mars, or he is from neither.
   - If Marvin is not from Earth, then Marvin is an extraterrestrial.

2. **Determine Marvin’s Origin**:
   - From the premise "Marvin is either from Earth and from Mars, or he is from neither," we need to consider both cases:
     - Case 1: Marvin is from Earth and from Mars.
     - Case 2: Marvin is from neither Earth nor Mars.

3. **Case 1: Marvin is from Earth and from Mars**:
   - If Marvin is from Earth, he is a human (since all highly intelligent beings from Earth are humans).
   - If Marvin is from Mars, he is an alien (by the second premise).

   Since Marvin cannot be both from Earth and from Mars simultaneously (as per the logical structure of the premises), this case is impossible.

4. **Case 2: Marvin is from neither Earth nor Mars**:
   - If Marvin is not from Earth, then according to the seventh premise, Marvin is an extraterrestrial.
   - Since all aliens are extraterrestrials (first premise), Marvin would be an alien.

5. **Conclusion**:
   - In both possible scenarios, Marvin is an extraterrestrial, and since all aliens are extraterrestrials, Marvin is an alien.

Therefore, the conclusion "Marvin is an alien" logically follows from the premises.

ANSWER: True
Processed: True

Reference: Uncertain

<PREMISES>

ANSWER:	Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona. From premise 1, we know that a La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another if it receives more points. From premise 4, we know that in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona. Therefore, in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona, so Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona, so the statement is true.
ANSWER:	True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate the statement "if Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel laureate". Let's assume that Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner. This doesn't tell us anything about whether Amy is a Nobel laureate, so the statement isn't true, meaning it is either False or Uncertain. To distinguish between the two, notice that we could have a scenario where Amy is neither an Olympic gold medal winner nor a Nobel laureate. None of the premises are violated in this case. This means the statement must be false.
ANSWER:	False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All aliens are extraterrestrials.
If someone is from Mars, then they are an alien.
No extraterrestrials are human.
All highly intelligent beings from Earth are humans.
Marvin is a highly intelligent being.
Marvin is either from Earth and from Mars, or he is from neither.
If Marvin is not from Earth, then Marvin is an extraterrestrial.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Marvin is neither a human nor from Mars.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
Let's analyze the premises and the conclusion step by step.

### Step-by-Step Analysis

1. **Premise 1**: All aliens are extraterrestrials.
   - \( \forall x (Alien(x) \rightarrow Extraterrestrial(x)) \)

2. **Premise 2**: If someone is from Mars, then they are an alien.
   - \( \forall x (FromMars(x) \rightarrow Alien(x)) \)

3. **Premise 3**: No extraterrestrials are human.
   - \( \forall x (Extraterrestrial(x) \rightarrow \neg Human(x)) \)

4. **Premise 4**: All highly intelligent beings from Earth are humans.
   - \( \forall x (HighlyIntelligent(x) \land FromEarth(x) \rightarrow Human(x)) \)

5. **Premise 5**: Marvin is a highly intelligent being.
   - \( HighlyIntelligent(Marvin) \)

6. **Premise 6**: Marvin is either from Earth and from Mars, or he is from neither.
   - \( (FromEarth(Marvin) \land FromMars(Marvin)) \lor \neg (FromEarth(Marvin) \lor FromMars(Marvin)) \)

7. **Premise 7**: If Marvin is not from Earth, then Marvin is an extraterrestrial.
   - \( \neg FromEarth(Marvin) \rightarrow Extraterrestrial(Marvin) \)

8. **Conclusion**: Marvin is neither a human nor from Mars.
   - \( \neg Human(Marvin) \land \neg FromMars(Marvin) \)

### Reasoning

1. **From Premise 5**: \( HighlyIntelligent(Marvin) \)
2. **From Premise 4**: Since Marvin is a highly intelligent being, if he is from Earth, he must be a human.
   - \( FromEarth(Marvin) \rightarrow Human(Marvin) \)

3. **From Premise 6**: \( (FromEarth(Marvin) \land FromMars(Marvin)) \lor \neg (FromEarth(Marvin) \lor FromMars(Marvin)) \)
   - This means either Marvin is from both Earth and Mars, or he is from neither.

4. **Case 1**: Suppose Marvin is from Earth.
   - Then from Premise 4, \( Human(Marvin) \).
   - But if Marvin is a human, he cannot be an extraterrestrial (from Premise 3).
   - Therefore, Marvin cannot be from Earth.

5. **Case 2**: Suppose Marvin is not from Earth.
   - From Premise 7, \( \neg FromEarth(Marvin) \rightarrow Extraterrestrial(Marvin) \), so \( Extraterrestrial(Marvin) \).
   - Since all extraterrestrials are not humans (Premise 3), \( \neg Human(Marvin) \).

6. **From Case 1 and Case 2**: Marvin cannot be from Earth, and since he is not from Earth, he must be an extraterrestrial.

7. **From Premise 6**: Since Marvin is not from Earth, he must be from Mars.
   - But if Marvin is from Mars, he must be an alien (Premise 2).
   - And if Marvin is an alien, he must be an extraterrestrial (Premise 1).
   - Therefore, Marvin is from Mars.

8. **Conclusion**: Marvin cannot be from Mars because we derived that he must be from Earth, which contradicts our assumption that he is not from Earth.

Since Marvin cannot be from Mars and we have shown that he must be from Mars, the conclusion that Marvin is neither a human nor from Mars is false.

### Final Answer:
**ANSWER: False**
Processed: False

Reference: True
========================================

     - Case 1: Marvin is from Earth and from Mars.

   - We need to check if this holds under the given premises.
   - From the analysis above, if Marvin is not from Mars, he could be from Earth (and thus a human) or from neither Earth nor Mars (and thus an extraterrestrial, not a human).

Given that Marvin cannot be from both Earth and Mars simultaneously, and if he is not from Mars, he could either be from Earth (a human) or from neither Earth nor Mars (an extraterrestrial), the conclusion does not necessarily hold universally. There is a scenario where Marvin is not from Mars and is not a human (e.g., he is from neither Earth nor Mars).

Therefore, the conclusion "If Marvin is not from Mars, then Marvin is a human" is not necessarily true based on the given premises.

From premise 1, we know that a La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another if it receives more points. From premise 4, we know that in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona. Therefore, in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona, so Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona, so the statement is true.
ANSWER:	True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate the statement "if Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel laureate". Let's assume that Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner. This doesn't tell us anything about whether Amy is a Nobel laureate, so the statement isn't true, meaning it is either False or Uncertain. To distinguish between the two, notice that we could have a scenario where Amy is neither an Olympic gold medal winner nor a Nobel laureate. None of the premises are violated in this case. This means the statement must be false.
ANSWER:	False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
Everyone at the mixer is a Grand Slam champion or an Oscar-nominated actor.
Every Grand Slam champion at the mixer is a professional tennis player.
All Oscar-nominated actors at the mixer are celebrities.
All professional tennis players at the mixer are athletes.
If a person at the mixer is a celebrity, then they are well paid.
If a person at the mixer is an athlete, then they are famous.
All well-paid people at the mixer live in tax havens.
Djokovic is at the mixer: if Djokovic is a famous athlete, then Djokovic is well-paid.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Djokovic is a Grand Slam champion.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
Let's analyze the premises step by step to determine if the conclusion "Djokovic is a Grand Slam champion" follows.

1. **Premise Analysis:**
   - Everyone at the mixer is a Grand Slam champion or an Oscar-nominated actor.
   - Every Grand Slam champion at the mixer is a professional tennis player.
   - All Oscar-nominated actors at the mixer are celebrities.
   - All professional tennis players at the mixer are athletes.
   - If a person at the mixer is a celebrity, then they are well paid.
   - If a person at the mixer is an athlete, then they are famous.
   - All well-paid people at the mixer live in tax havens.
   - Djokovic is at the mixer: if Djokovic is a famous athlete, then Djokovic is well-paid.

2. **Determine Djokovic’s Status:**
   - Since Djokovic is at the mixer, he is either a Grand Slam champion or an Oscar-nominated actor.
   - If Djokovic is a Grand Slam champion, then he is a professional tennis player (from Premise 2).
   - If Djokovic is an Oscar-nominated actor, he is a celebrity (from Premise 3), and thus well-paid (from Premise 5).

3. **Consider the Conclusion:**
   - The conclusion states "Djokovic is a Grand Slam champion."
   - We need to check if this can be logically deduced from the premises.

4. **Analyze the Given Information:**
   - If Djokovic is a Grand Slam champion, he fits the description perfectly.
   - However, we do not have any information that definitively excludes the possibility that Djokovic could be an Oscar-nominated actor instead.

5. **Evaluate the Possibilities:**
   - If Djokovic is an Oscar-nominated actor, he would still fit the criteria of being at the mixer (since everyone is either a Grand Slam champion or an Oscar-nominated actor).
   - There is no contradiction in assuming Djokovic could be an Oscar-nominated actor and still be at the mixer.

6. **Conclusion:**
   - While Djokovic could be a Grand Slam champion, the premises do not provide enough information to conclusively state that he is one. He could also be an Oscar-nominated actor, which does not contradict any of the premises.

Therefore, the conclusion "Djokovic is a Grand Slam champion" cannot be definitively derived from the given premises.

**ANSWER: Uncertain**
Processed: Uncertain

Reference: Uncertain

Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions, Provide your reasoning step by step and conclude with 'ANSWER:	True', 'ANSWER:	False', or 'ANSWER:	Uncertain'.


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if a worksheet is not dispensable. From premise 6, we know that a worksheet is either paper or is environment-friendly. If it is paper, then from premise 3, a worksheet is woodware, and from premise 2, a worksheet is dispensable. If it is environment-friendly, we know it is good from premise 5, but we know nothing about whether it is dispensable. Therefore, we don't know if a worksheet is dispensible or not, so the statement is uncertain.
ANSWER:	Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

From premise 1, we know that a La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another if it receives more points. From premise 4, we know that in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona. Therefore, in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona, so Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona, so the statement is true.
ANSWER:	True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.

If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>

This doesn't tell us anything about whether Amy is a Nobel laureate, so the statement isn't true, meaning it is either False or Uncertain. To distinguish between the two, notice that we could have a scenario where Amy is neither an Olympic gold medal winner nor a Nobel laureate. None of the premises are violated in this case. This means the statement must be false.
ANSWER:	False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
Everyone at the mixer is a Grand Slam champion or an Oscar-nominated actor.
Every Grand Slam champion at the mixer is a professional tennis player.
All Oscar-nominated actors at the mixer are celebrities.
All professional tennis players at the mixer are athletes.
If a person at the mixer is a celebrity, then they are well paid.
If a person at the mixer is an athlete, then they are famous.
All well-paid people at the mixer live in tax havens.
Djokovic is at the mixer: if Djokovic is a famous athlete, then Djokovic is well-paid.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Djokovic lives in a tax haven.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
Let's analyze the premises and the conclusion step by step.

1. **Premise Analysis**:
   - Everyone at the mixer is a Grand Slam champion or an Oscar-nominated actor.
   - Every Grand Slam champion at the mixer is a professional tennis player.
   - All Oscar-nominated actors at the mixer are celebrities.
   - All professional tennis players at the mixer are athletes.
   - If a person at the mixer is a celebrity, then they are well paid.
   - If a person at the mixer is an athlete, then they are famous.
   - All well-paid people at the mixer live in tax havens.
   - Djokovic is at the mixer: if Djokovic is a famous athlete, then Djokovic is well-paid.

2. **Determine Djokovic's Status**:
   - Since Djokovic is at the mixer, he is either a Grand Slam champion or an Oscar-nominated actor.
   - If Djokovic is a Grand Slam champion, he is a professional tennis player (from Premise 2).
   - If Djokovic is an Oscar-nominated actor, he is a celebrity (from Premise 3).

3. **Evaluate the Conclusion**:
   - The conclusion states: "Djokovic lives in a tax haven."
   - For Djokovic to live in a tax haven, he needs to be well-paid (from Premise 7).
   - To be well-paid, Djokovic needs to be a celebrity (from Premise 5), or he needs to be an athlete (from Premise 6).

4. **Analyze Possible Scenarios**:
   - **Scenario 1**: Djokovic is a Grand Slam champion.
     - He is a professional tennis player (Premise 2).
     - He is an athlete (from being a professional tennis player).
     - Being an athlete, he is famous (Premise 6).
     - Being famous, he might be well-paid (not explicitly stated, but implied as a possibility for famous athletes).
     - If Djokovic is well-paid, he lives in a tax haven (Premise 7).

   - **Scenario 2**: Djokovic is an Oscar-nominated actor.
     - He is a celebrity (Premise 3).
     - Being a celebrity, he is well-paid (Premise 5).
     - Being well-paid, he lives in a tax haven (Premise 7).

5. **Conclusion**:
   - In both scenarios, Djokovic can be well-paid and thus live in a tax haven.
   - There is no information provided that contradicts these scenarios.

Therefore, based on the given premises, it is reasonable to conclude that Djokovic lives in a tax haven.

ANSWER: True
Processed: True

Reference: True

All well-paid people at the mixer live in tax havens.
Djokovic is at the mixer: if Djokovic is a famous athlete, then Djokovic is well-paid.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Djokovic does not live in a tax haven.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if Djokovic does not live in a tax haven.

First, let's break down the premises:

1. Everyone at the mixer is a Grand Slam champion or an Oscar-nominated actor.
2. Every Grand Slam champion at the mixer is a professional tennis player.
3. All Oscar-nominated actors at the mixer are celebrities.
4. All professional tennis players at the mixer are athletes.
5. If a person at the mixer is a celebrity, then they are well paid.
6. If a person at the mixer is an athlete, then they are famous.
7. All well-paid people at the mixer live in tax havens.
8. Djokovic is at the mixer: if Djokovic is a famous athlete, then Djokovic is well-paid.

Now, let's analyze the information about Djokovic:

- Since Djokovic is at the mixer, he is either a Grand Slam champion or an Oscar-nominated actor (Premise 1).
- If Djokovic is a Grand Slam champion, then he is a professional tennis player (Premise 2), and therefore an athlete (Premise 4). If Djokovic is an Oscar-nominated actor, he is a celebrity (Premise 3).
- If Djokovic is a celebrity, then he is well paid (Premise 5).
- If Djokovic is an athlete, then he is famous (Premise 6).

Given Premise 8, if Djokovic is a famous athlete, then Djokovic is well-paid. 

From Premise 7, all well-paid people at the mixer live in tax havens. Therefore, if Djokovic is well-paid, he lives in a tax haven.

Since Djokovic can either be a famous athlete or a celebrity (or both), and in either case, he would be well-paid and thus live in a tax haven, we can conclude that Djokovic does live in a tax haven.

Therefore, the conclusion "Djokovic does not live in a tax haven" is false.

ANSWER: False
Processed: False

Reference: False

<PREMISES>
All of Zaha Hadid's design styles that Max adores have interesting geometries.
No brutalist buildings that Max adores have interesting geometries.
Every style that Max adores is either Zaha Hadid's design style or Kelly Wearstler's design style.
All of Kelly Wearstler's design styles that Max adores are evocative.
All of Kelly Wearstler's design styles that Max adores are dreamy.
If a design by Max that he adores has interesting geometries, then the design is a brutalist building and evocative.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A design by Max is a brutalist building.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if a design by Max is a brutalist building.

1. **Premise Analysis**:
   - All of Zaha Hadid's design styles that Max adores have interesting geometries.
   - No brutalist buildings that Max adores have interesting geometries.
   - Every style that Max adores is either Zaha Hadid's design style or Kelly Wearstler's design style.
   - All of Kelly Wearstler's design styles that Max adores are evocative.
   - All of Kelly Wearstler's design styles that Max adores are dreamy.
   - If a design by Max that he adores has interesting geometries, then the design is a brutalist building and evocative.

2. **Logical Breakdown**:
   - From the first premise, any design by Max that he adores and has interesting geometries must be a brutalist building.
   - From the second premise, no brutalist buildings that Max adores can have interesting geometries.
   - From the third premise, every style that Max adores is either a Zaha Hadid design or a Kelly Wearstler design.
   - From the fourth and fifth premises, all Kelly Wearstler designs that Max adores are evocative and dreamy, and they do not have interesting geometries.
   - The sixth premise states that if a design by Max that he adores has interesting geometries, then it is a brutalist building and evocative.

3. **Conclusion Analysis**:
   - Since no brutalist buildings that Max adores can have interesting geometries, and if a design by Max that he adores has interesting geometries, it must be a brutalist building, we need to consider the implications.
   - If Max adores a brutalist building, it cannot have interesting geometries according to the second premise.
   - However, if Max adores a design with interesting geometries, it must be a brutalist building according to the sixth premise.
   - Given that no brutalist building that Max adores can have interesting geometries, the only way for a design by Max to be a brutalist building is if it does not have interesting geometries.

4. **Final Consideration**:
   - Since the premises do not provide any direct information about whether Max adores a brutalist building without interesting geometries, we cannot definitively conclude that a design by Max is a brutalist building based solely on the given premises.

Therefore, the statement "A design by Max is a brutalist building" is not necessarily true based on the given premises.

ANSWER: Uncertain
Processed: Uncertain

Reference: Uncertain
